<GmapID>0x809b20384543708d:0x37cc0fc2e9476b27</GmapID><text>First off I wanna start by saying that I am 19 and as being a part of the young generation I like good internet service. Consolidated Communications is not one of them. Previously the company surewest supplied our home with internet and phone and have since been bought out by consolidated. Surewest was by no means anazing but the servhce was far better than consolidated service. I've taken it upon myself to consistently check Consolidated's speed and found that service you recieve is in pulses.

Think of taking a shower but your water comes out as if you were pumping it by hand. Now for most people this might seem ok but if you have anyone living in your household under 25 you will most likely be hearing complaints. These pulses will freeze your HD video and prevent you from doing things online that require continuous data such as playing online games or downloading large files.

Secondly, there customer service is horrible. The person you get to help you is hit or miss but they really can't help you outside of teaching you how to plug in the modem to your wall. You can argue all you want all theyll do is say you should buy a faster internet speed which will amount to nothing because they advertise their speeds as *up to* meaning if you recieve slower speeds than that if which you paid it is all part of the deal. And you definitley will get slower speeds.

Lastly, this may not matter to most but because consolidated still uses the old telephone wires underground, meaning you must be connected to a modem. "This is the alternative to being connected to the more modern wiring system which is called fiber. Fiber is much faster and more reliable but is not available in many areas around roseville." Now normally being connected to a modem is only a small inconvenience however they have this modem completely locked down. They dont allow you to have access to change any of the settings whether that be setting automatic resets or port forwarding.

So Consolidated Communications is going to recieve a 1 star from me. The service itself is horrible and the customer service is completley useless unless you don't know how to plug a cable into a wall. I would stick to tethering from your phone its faster and more reliable...

TLDR: Consolidated has horrible internet service and offers you no other alternative plan. You can pay more but it will do nothing. Unless you only check emails and like to watch less than HD video with the occasional buffer this Internet is not for you.

P.S. To those who choose to disregard this review, please consider paying for one of Consolidateds cheaper plans as paying more will only get them more revenue and barely add any benefit to you. As someone who likes to push internet service to its limits the Trade Off is most definitley not a fair one.< /text>< rating>

Roseville Telephone Co. Was the original phone co. Started by Bob Doyle.  He'd roll over in his grave if he knew the company merged with a sloppy company.  In 2002-2003, Roseville Telco CHANGED the name to SureWest in order to brand the products as mainstream rather than the old fashioned POTS phone lines.
My experience with Consolidated is that when I called to get my service xfered, the customer service rep said "oh good, we don't service that part of Roseville!  Thanks, bye ((click))".  She was very upbeat and Relieved about not having to xfer service!  I know that most of the original employees are gone, you don't get the same good customer service you used to.  I just called their number while they're closed: Instead of saying they're closed and giving the hours of operation, they make you go thru a phone tree.  Once you get to the dep't you want, the recording says "please leave a voicemail or call back later."  How rude!  Why should someone go thru all that trouble just to be told to leave. VM, and for Whom??  Not impressed at all with their company.</Review>

<rating>5<//rating><text>When it's chilly and rainy out and you're feeling a bit "under the weather" - Vietnamese rice porridge (chao) is probably one of the best comfort foods you can get in the area. Chao is as warm and comforting as American "chicken noodle soup". It is easy to eat, easy to garnish with a variety of different meat options and filling.

I'll typically phone in my order and pick up rather than eat inside, although I definitely like their renovations as there is a lot more space to eat vs. how the interior used to look like when they first opened (a few picnic tables and plastic chairs).

My favorite to order here is the Chao Bo Bam + Century Egg (Beef rice porridge). I always ask for extra ginger since it helps clear up the sinuses/nasal passages. Since I typically come in the evening, there isn't anymore fresh chinese doughnuts - but if you have a chance, definitely order some to dip in your porridge.

Parking is a nightmare as usual (as it is Little Saigon) - but go at night near closing time and there is plenty of parking.

Cash only - I believe they take CC as well but with a hefty minimum ($20 or something like that - so mostly for their cake orders). Prices here are reasonable and have not increased much due to inflation.< /text><Pics>None</Pics><response>None<//response><Gmap_id>0x80dd27b5e9afa06b:0xbf8e8f44f7496881<//Gmap_id></record>
